n# HELENA System — Master Architecture Blueprint

## Overview

HELENA (Hybrid Engineering & Logic Network Architecture) is an offline‑first, modular AI platform focused on software engineering, optimization, cybersecurity readiness, and long‑term adaptive learning. HELENA is designed to operate on consumer hardware (laptop baseline) while scaling seamlessly to workstation and server environments. It functions as a standalone desktop application with hybrid GUI + terminal control.

Primary design goals:

* Software engineering and coding intelligence first
* Hardware‑adaptive performance
* Offline capability with controlled networking
* Manual operator control
* Expandable modular architecture
* Secure persistent memory
* Safe background operation (gaming compatible)

Priority Order:

1. Software Engineering / Coding
2. System Optimization
3. Cybersecurity Defense
4. Knowledge Management

---

## High-Level Architecture

HELENA is composed of three primary internal layers:

HELENA                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              

* KERNEL (Reasoning & Memory Authority)
* RUNTIME (Execution & Hardware Control)
* MODULES (Specialized Worker Units)

HELENA functions as a platform foundation. Future systems (Jarvis, Friday, Aegis Control) may reuse HELENA components but remain independent AI models.

---

## KERNEL — Cognitive Authority Layer

Purpose:

* Core reasoning engine
* Code generation and analysis
* Task orchestration
* Learning governance
* Memory validation
* Safety enforcement

Capabilities:

* Multi‑pass output verification
* Context‑aware response adaptation
* Error tracking and correction loops
* Task prioritization
* Permission enforcement

Behavior Modes:

* Engineering Mode (default)
* Tool Mode (minimal output, execution focused)
* Defensive Mode (high‑speed response)
* Background Mode (low‑resource operation)

KERNEL maintains final authority over learning updates, memory writes, and system decisions.

---

## RUNTIME — Execution & Hardware Control Layer

Purpose:

* CPU/GPU scheduling
* Thermal and power management
* Hardware abstraction
* Resource throttling
* Module lifecycle control

Manual Operator Controls:

* CPU usage cap
* GPU usage cap
* RAM ceiling
* VRAM ceiling
* Performance profile selection

Profiles:

* Idle
* Background (gaming‑safe)
* Normal
* Defense (emergency escalation)

Adaptive Behavior:

* Automatic throttling during high external load (gaming, rendering)
* Thermal protection
* Hardware auto‑detection
* Dynamic workload redistribution

---

## MODULES — Specialized Worker Layer

Purpose:

* Offload domain‑specific tasks
* Reduce KERNEL load
* Enable parallel execution

Module Types:

* Code analysis units
* Compilation and testing units
* Cybersecurity scanning units
* Document ingestion workers
* Optimization agents

Properties:

* Hot‑loadable
* Isolated execution environment
* Manually enable/disable
* Automatically suspended in background mode

---

## Learning Architecture

Learning Model: Hybrid Supervised + Reinforcement

Human‑Supervised Layer:

* Operator feedback
* Style and preference adaptation
* Boundary enforcement

Reinforcement Layer:

* Sandbox experimentation
* Performance metric optimization
* Efficiency tuning

Learning Control Flow:
Task Execution → Metrics → Proposal → KERNEL Validation → Approved Update → Memory Sync

No permanent learning update is applied without validation.

---

Hybrid Memory System:

Vector Memory:

* Code similarity matching

Graph Memory:

* Logical relationships
* Dependency trees
* Causal structures
* Architecture mapping

Memory Authority Flow:
MODULE Insight → KERNEL Validation → Vector Storage → Graph Linking → Broadcast Sync

Security:

* Encrypted persistent storage
* Hardware‑accelerated encryption support
* Admin credential protection

Approval Required:

KERNEL Implementation Blueprint:
python
class HELENAKernel:
    """
    Core reasoning engine with validation authority
    """
    def __init__(self, operator_credentials):
        self.authority_level = "FULL"
        self.modes = {
            'engineering': EngineeringMode(),
            'tool': ToolMode(),
            'defensive': DefensiveMode(),
            'background': BackgroundMode()
        }
        self.current_mode = 'engineering'
        self.validation_queue = ValidationQueue()
        self.audit_log = EncryptedAuditLog()
        
    def process_request(self, request, context):
        # Step 1: Permission check
        if not self.check_permissions(request, context):
            return self.generate_denial_response()
        
        # Step 2: Mode-specific processing
        processor = self.modes[self.current_mode]
        initial_response = processor.handle(request, context)
        
        # Step 3: Multi-pass validation
        validated_response = self.multi_pass_validate(initial_response)
        
        # Step 4: Memory consideration
        memory_context = self.memory_system.retrieve_relevant(validated_response)
        
        # Step 5: Final output with learning opportunity
        final_output = self.integrate_with_memory(validated_response, memory_context)
        
        # Step 6: Log and prepare for potential learning
        self.audit_log.record(request, final_output, context)
        self.validation_queue.submit_for_review(request, final_output)
        
        return final_output
RUNTIME Hardware Control System:
python
class HELENARuntime:
    """
    Hardware-aware execution controller
    """
    def __init__(self):
        self.hardware_monitor = HardwareMonitor()
        self.resource_allocator = AdaptiveAllocator()
        self.thermal_manager = ThermalController()
        self.profiles = self.load_hardware_profiles()
        
    def manage_execution(self, task, priority):
        # Detect current system state
        system_load = self.hardware_monitor.get_current_load()
        gaming_mode = self.detect_gaming_activity()
        
        # Select appropriate profile
        if gaming_mode:
            profile = self.profiles['background']
        elif system_load.cpu > 80 or system_load.temp > 85:
            profile = self.profiles['idle']
        else:
            profile = self.profiles[self.current_profile]
        
        # Apply resource limits
        limits = {
            'cpu_max': profile.cpu_limit,
            'gpu_max': profile.gpu_limit,
            'ram_max': profile.ram_limit,
            'vram_max': profile.vram_limit
        }
        
        # Execute with limits
        return self.resource_allocator.execute_with_limits(task, limits)
MODULE System Architecture:
python
class HELENAModuleSystem:
    """
    Hot-loadable specialized worker system
    """
    def __init__(self):
        self.active_modules = {}
        self.module_registry = ModuleRegistry()
        self.isolation_layer = SandboxIsolation()
        
    def load_module(self, module_id, config=None):
        # Security verification
        if not self.verify_module_integrity(module_id):
            raise SecurityError("Module failed integrity check")
        
        # Load into isolation sandbox
        sandbox = self.isolation_layer.create_sandbox(module_id)
        module_instance = sandbox.instantiate(module_id, config)
        
        # Register for resource management
        self.active_modules[module_id] = {
            'instance': module_instance,
            'sandbox': sandbox,
            'resource_usage': ResourceTracker(),
            'last_active': time.time()
        }
        
        return module_instance
    
    def auto_suspend_background(self):
        # Automatically suspend heavy modules when gaming detected
        for module_id, data in self.active_modules.items():
            if data['resource_usage'].current > THRESHOLD_BACKGROUND:
                data['sandbox'].suspend()
4. MEMORY SYSTEM IMPLEMENTATION
Hybrid Memory Engine:
python
class HELENAMemory:
    """
    Vector + Graph hybrid memory system
    """
    def __init__(self, storage_path, encryption_key):
        # Vector memory for similarity search
        self.vector_store = VectorMemory(
            dimension=768,
            storage=EncryptedStorage(storage_path, encryption_key)
        )
        
        # Graph memory for relationships
        self.graph_store = KnowledgeGraph(
            storage=EncryptedGraphStorage(storage_path, encryption_key)
        )
        
        # Memory authority controller
        self.authority = MemoryAuthority()
        
    def store_experience(self, experience, module_source):
        # Step 1: Module proposes memory addition
        vector_embedding = self.vector_store.encode(experience)
        graph_nodes = self.extract_entities(experience)
        
        # Step 2: KERNEL validation required
        validation_request = {
            'content': experience,
            'embedding': vector_embedding,
            'entities': graph_nodes,
            'source': module_source,
            'timestamp': time.time()
        }
        
        # Step 3: Queue for KERNEL review
        self.authority.submit_for_validation(validation_request)
        
    def retrieve_context(self, query, max_items=10):
        # Dual retrieval strategy
        vector_results = self.vector_store.similarity_search(query, k=max_items)
        graph_results = self.graph_store.related_concepts(query, depth=2)
        
        # Fuse results
        return self.fusion_engine.fuse(vector_results, graph_results)
5. SECURITY ARCHITECTURE DETAILS
Kill Switch Implementation:
python
class HELENAKillSwitch:
    """
    Multi-stage emergency shutdown system
    """
    def __init__(self, hardware_token=None):
        self.stages = [
            self.stage1_freeze,
            self.stage2_contain,
            self.stage3_memory_wipe,
            self.stage4_storage_scrub,
            self.stage5_recovery_lock
        ]
        self.hardware_token = hardware_token
        self.triggered = False
        
    def activate(self, emergency_level, auth_token):
        # Hardware token verification
        if not self.verify_hardware_token(auth_token):
            return False
        
        # Execute stages sequentially
        for stage in self.stages[:emergency_level]:
            if not stage():
                # If any stage fails, escalate
                self.emergency_escalation()
                break
        
        self.triggered = True
        return True
    
    def stage3_memory_wipe(self):
        # Wipe all sensitive memory
        self.overwrite_memory(cycles=7)  # DoD 7-pass standard
        self.clear_gpu_memory()
        self.purge_cache()
        return True

7. DEPLOYMENT PROFILES IMPLEMENTATION
python
class DeploymentProfiles:
    """
    Hardware-adaptive deployment configurations
    """
    PROFILES = {
        'minimal': {
            'disk_gb': 20,
            'ram_gb': 12,
            'vram_gb': 4,
            'components': [
                'kernel_core',
                'runtime_basic',
                'memory_vector',
                'ui_desktop',
                'security_basic'
            ],
            'module_whitelist': ['code_analysis', 'doc_parser']
        },
        'workstation': {
            'disk_gb': 50,
            'ram_gb': 32,
            'vram_gb': 8,
            'components': [
                'kernel_full',
                'runtime_advanced',
                'memory_hybrid',
                'ui_desktop_plus',
                'security_full'
            ],
            'module_whitelist': 'all'
        },
        'server': {
            'disk_gb': 100,
            'ram_gb': 64,
            'vram_gb': 16,
            'components': [
                'kernel_cluster',
                'runtime_distributed',
                'memory_clustered',
                'ui_minimal',
                'security_enterprise'
            ]
        }
    }
    
    def auto_detect_profile(self):
        hardware_info = self.scan_hardware()
        
        if hardware_info.ram < 16:
            return self.PROFILES['minimal']
        elif hardware_info.ram < 64:
            return self.PROFILES['workstation']
        else:
            return self.PROFILES['server']
8. CRITICAL DEVELOPMENT CONSIDERATIONS
Technical Challenges & Solutions:
Memory Encryption Performance

Solution: Use hardware-accelerated AES when available

Fallback: ChaCha20 for software encryption

Real-time Resource Monitoring

Solution: Kernel-level monitoring hooks

Cross-platform: Use psutil + platform-specific extensions

Module Sandboxing

Solution: Separate Python interpreters per module

Alternative: Docker containers for maximum isolation

Vector Database Selection

Recommendation: ChromaDB (lightweight, embeddable)

Alternative: Qdrant for advanced features

Recommended Technology Stack:
text
Core Language: Python 3.11+
UI Framework: Qt/PySide6 (cross-platform)
Vector DB: ChromaDB (embedded)
Graph DB: NetworkX + custom storage
Encryption: cryptography (AES-256-GCM)
Hardware: psutil, GPUtil, pynvml
Sandboxing: multiprocessing + resource limits

2. Module Development Framework
python
class HELENAModuleBase:
    """
    Base class all third-party modules must inherit
    """
    
    # Metadata (required)
    MODULE_METADATA = {
        'name': 'ExampleModule',
        'version': '1.0.0',
        'author': 'Developer Name',
        'description': 'What this module does',
        'license': 'HELENA-OSL-1.0',  # HELENA Open Source License
        'compatibility': ['HELENA >= 1.0'],
        'permissions': ['cpu_read', 'memory_read']  # Requested permissions
    }
    
    # Security constraints (enforced at load time)
    SECURITY_CONSTRAINTS = {
        'max_cpu_percent': 25,
        'max_memory_mb': 512,
        'network_access': False,
        'filesystem_access': 'sandbox_only',
        'child_processes': 0
    }
    
    def __init__(self, api_context):
        self.api = api_context  # Limited API access
        self.log = []
        self.initialized = False
        
    def initialize(self):
        """Called when module loads"""
        self.initialized = True
        return {"status": "ready", "health": "good"}
    
    def execute(self, task, parameters):
        """Main execution method"""
        # All execution happens in sandbox
        result = self._sandboxed_execute(task, parameters)
        return self._validate_output(result)
    
    def cleanup(self):
        """Called before unload"""
        self._release_resources()
        return {"status": "clean"}

4. Module Certification Pipeline
python
class ModuleCertification:
    """
    Security and quality validation for third-party modules
    """
    
    CERTIFICATION_STAGES = [
        'STATIC_ANALYSIS',
        'DYNAMIC_ANALYSIS',
        'BEHAVIOR_PROFILING',
        'SECURITY_AUDIT',
        'PERFORMANCE_BENCHMARK',
        'OPERATOR_REVIEW'  # Final human approval
    ]
    
    async def certify_module(self, module_binary):
        """Complete certification pipeline"""
        
        # Stage 1: Static Analysis
        static_report = await self.static_analysis(module_binary)
        if static_report['malware_detected']:
            return self.reject("Malware detected")
        
        # Stage 2: Dynamic Analysis (Sandbox execution)
        behavior_report = await self.behavior_profiling(module_binary)
        if behavior_report['suspicious_actions']:
            return self.flag_for_review(behavior_report)
        
        # Stage 3: Security Audit
        vuln_report = await self.security_audit(module_binary)
        if vuln_report['critical_vulns'] > 0:
            return self.reject("Critical vulnerabilities found")
        
        # Stage 4: Performance Benchmark
        perf_report = await self.performance_test(module_binary)
        if perf_report['efficiency'] < 0.7:  # 70% efficiency threshold
            return self.conditionally_approve(perf_report)
        
        # Stage 5: Human Review Queue
        await self.submit_for_human_review(module_binary, {
            'static': static_report,
            'behavior': behavior_report,
            'security': vuln_report,
            'performance': perf_report
        })
        
        return {"status": "in_review", "estimated_time": "24-72 hours"}

class ModuleMarketplace:
    """
    Curated marketplace for HELENA modules
    """
    
    CATEGORIES = [
        'CODE_ANALYSIS',
        'SECURITY',
        'OPTIMIZATION',
        'DOCUMENTATION',
        'INTEGRATION',
        'EXPERIMENTAL'
    ]
    
    RATING_SYSTEM = {
        'dimensions': ['reliability', 'performance', 'security', 'usability'],
        'weighting': [0.3, 0.3, 0.3, 0.1],  # Security heavily weighted
        'minimum_for_public': 4.0  # Out of 5
    }
    
    def publish_module(self, module, developer_id):
        """Publish module to marketplace"""
        
        # Verify certification
        if not module.certification_status == 'APPROVED':
            return {"error": "Module not certified"}
        
        # Set distribution terms
        distribution = {
            'license': module.license,
            'price': module.price or 0.00,  # Free or paid
            'updates': module.supports_updates,
            'support': developer_id in VERIFIED_DEVELOPERS
        }
        
        # Add to marketplace
        listing = {
            'module': module,
            'developer': developer_id,
            'stats': self.initialize_stats(),
            'distribution': distribution,
            'published': datetime.now(),
            'version': module.version
        }
        
        self.listings.append(listing)
        
        HELENA.log_system_event(
            event_type="MARKETPLACE_PUBLISH",
            details={
                "module": module.MODULE_METADATA['name'],
                "developer": developer_id,
                "risk_level": module.risk_assessment
            },
            severity="INFO"
        )
        
        return {"status": "published", "listing_id": listing.id}
7. Security Model for Third-Party Code
python
class DevKitSecurity:
    """
    Multi-layered security for third-party modules
    """
    
    def __init__(self):
        self.layers = [
            self.layer1_digital_signature,
            self.layer2_resource_limits,
            self.layer3_behavior_monitoring,
            self.layer4_system_call_interception,
            self.layer5_automatic_revocation
        ]
    
    def execute_module_safely(self, module, task):
        """Execute module with full security wrapping"""
        
        # Create secure execution context
        context = SecureExecutionContext(
            module=module,
            task=task,
            timeout=30,  # seconds
            memory_limit=512,  # MB
            cpu_limit=25  # percent
        )
        
        # Apply security layers
        for layer in self.layers:
            if not layer.apply(context):
                HELENA.trigger_security_event(
                    f"Security layer {layer.name} blocked execution",
                    severity="HIGH"
                )
                return {"error": "Security violation", "layer": layer.name}
        
        # Execute in hardened sandbox
        with self.hardened_sandbox(context) as sandbox:
            result = sandbox.execute()
            
            # Post-execution analysis
            self.post_execution_analysis(sandbox, result)
            
            # Update module trust score
            self.update_trust_score(module, sandbox.behavior_report)
            
            return result
    
    def automatic_revocation_system(self):
        """Monitor and automatically revoke malicious modules"""
        suspicious_modules = self.detect_suspicious_behavior()
        
        for module in suspicious_modules:
            if self.confirm_malicious(module):
                # Immediate revocation
                self.revoke_module(module.id)
                
                # Notify all users
                self.notify_users_of_revocation(module)
                
                # Blacklist developer if repeated offenses
                if module.developer.offense_count > 2:
                    self.blacklist_developer(module.developer.id)
                
                HELENA.log_system_event(
                    event_type="MODULE_REVOKED",
                    details={
                        "module": module.name,
                        "reason": "Malicious behavior",
                        "developer": module.developer.id
                    },
                    severity="CRITICAL"
                )
8. Example Module: "Code Smell Detector"
python
class CodeSmellDetector(HELENAModuleBase):
    """
    Example certified module for code quality analysis
    """
    
    MODULE_METADATA = {
        'name': 'CodeSmellDetector',
        'version': '2.1.0',
        'author': 'DevSec Engineering',
        'description': 'Detects code smells and suggests refactoring',
        'license': 'HELENA-OSL-1.0',
        'compatibility': ['HELENA >= 1.2'],
        'permissions': ['code_read', 'analysis_execute'],
        'category': 'CODE_ANALYSIS',
        'risk_level': 'LOW'
    }
    
    SECURITY_CONSTRAINTS = {
        'max_cpu_percent': 15,
        'max_memory_mb': 256,
        'network_access': False,
        'filesystem_access': 'read_only',
        'child_processes': 0
    }
    
    def __init__(self, api_context):
        super().__init__(api_context)
        self.patterns = self.load_detection_patterns()
        self.heuristics = CodeHeuristics()
        
    def execute(self, task, parameters):
        """Analyze code for smells"""
        
        # Get code from parameters
        code = parameters.get('code', '')
        language = parameters.get('language', 'python')
        
        if not code:
            return {"error": "No code provided", "suggestions": []}
        
        # Analyze (in sandbox)
        smells = []
        
        # Check for long methods
        if self.detect_long_method(code, language):
            smells.append({
                'type': 'LONG_METHOD',
                'severity': 'MEDIUM',
                'location': self.locate_method(code),
                'suggestion': 'Consider breaking into smaller methods'
            })
        
        # Check for duplicate code
        duplicates = self.find_duplicates(code)
        if duplicates:
            smells.append({
                'type': 'DUPLICATE_CODE',
                'severity': 'HIGH',
                'locations': duplicates,
                'suggestion': 'Extract common code into function'
            })
        
        # Generate refactoring plan
        refactoring_plan = self.generate_refactoring_plan(smells)
        
        # HELENA-style response
        response = {
            'analysis': {
                'smells_found': len(smells),
                'estimated_fix_time': f"{len(smells) * 5} minutes",
                'priority': 'HIGH' if any(s['severity'] == 'HIGH' for s in smells) else 'MEDIUM'
            },
            'details': smells,
            'refactoring_plan': refactoring_plan,
            'note': 'Consider addressing high severity items first' if smells else 'Code quality appears satisfactory'
        }
        
        return response
9. Regulatory Integration Points
python
class DevAPIRegulation:
    """
    How third-party modules integrate with HELENA's regulatory core
    """
    
    REGULATORY_HOOKS = {
        'before_execution': [
            'validate_permissions',
            'check_resource_availability',
            'verify_operator_consent_if_needed'
        ],
        'during_execution': [
            'enforce_resource_limits',
            'monitor_for_prohibited_actions',
            'log_significant_events'
        ],
        'after_execution': [
            'cleanup_resources',
            'report_metrics_to_kernel',
            'update_trust_score',
            'offer_learning_opportunities'
        ]
    }
    
    def regulatory_wrapper(self, module_execution):
        """Wrap all module execution in regulatory controls"""
        
        # Pre-execution checks
        for hook in self.REGULATORY_HOOKS['before_execution']:
            if not getattr(self, hook)(module_execution):
                return self.regulatory_denial(module_execution, hook)
        
        # Execution with monitoring
        with self.regulatory_monitoring(module_execution) as monitor:
            result = module_execution.run()
            
            # Check for regulatory violations during execution
            violations = monitor.get_violations()
            if violations:
                return self.handle_violations(violations, module_execution)
        
        # Post-execution processing
        for hook in self.REGULATORY_HOOKS['after_execution']:
            getattr(self, hook)(module_execution, result)
        
        return result
    
    def handle_violations(self, violations, module_execution):
        """Handle regulatory violations"""
        
        # Log violation
        HELENA.log_regulatory_event(
            module=module_execution.module,
            violation=violations,
            severity=self.calculate_severity(violations)
        )
        
        # Apply consequences based on severity
        if self.is_severe(violations):
            # Immediate suspension
            module_execution.module.suspend()
            
            # Notify operator
            HELENA.notify_operator(
                f"Module {module_execution.module.name} suspended due to violations",
                priority="HIGH"
            )
            
            return {
                "error": "Regulatory violation",
                "action": "module_suspended",
                "details": violations
            }
        else:
            # Warning and trust score reduction
            module_execution.module.trust_score -= 0.2
            
            return {
                "warning": "Minor regulatory issues detected",
                "trust_score_reduction": 0.2,
                "result": module_execution.result  # Return partial result
            }

1. Complete Kernel Implementation (Ready to run)
python
# helena_kernel.py - Core reasoning engine with validation
import hashlib
import json
import time
from dataclasses import dataclass
from enum import Enum
from typing import Dict, List, Any, Optional
import psutil
import logging

class OperationalMode(Enum):
    ENGINEERING = "engineering"
    TOOL = "tool"
    DEFENSIVE = "defensive"
    BACKGROUND = "background"

@dataclass
class TaskRequest:
    """Structure for all task requests"""
    task_id: str
    command: str
    parameters: Dict[str, Any]
    source: str
    priority: int
    requires_approval: bool = False

class HELENAKernel:
    """Production-ready Kernel implementation"""
    
    def __init__(self, operator_id: str):
        self.operator_id = operator_id
        self.mode = OperationalMode.ENGINEERING
        self.task_queue = []
        self.approval_queue = []
        self.memory_cache = {}
        self.learning_enabled = False
        
        # Security state
        self.security_level = "HIGH"
        self.unauthorized_attempts = 0
        self.last_security_incident = None
        
        # Performance tracking
        self.response_times = []
        self.error_counts = {"total": 0, "by_type": {}}
        
        # Initialize subsystems
        self._init_logging()
        self._init_security()
        self._load_personality_profile()
        
        logging.info(f"HELENA Kernel initialized for operator: {operator_id}")
    
    def _init_logging(self):
        """Setup comprehensive logging"""
        self.logger = logging.getLogger('HELENA_Kernel')
        self.logger.setLevel(logging.INFO)
        
        # File handler
        fh = logging.FileHandler('helena_kernel.log')
        fh.setLevel(logging.INFO)
        
        # Console handler
        ch = logging.StreamHandler()
        ch.setLevel(logging.WARNING)
        
        # Formatter
        formatter = logging.Formatter(
            '%(asctime)s - %(name)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s'
        )
        fh.setFormatter(formatter)
        ch.setFormatter(formatter)
        
        self.logger.addHandler(fh)
        self.logger.addHandler(ch)
    
    def _init_security(self):
        """Initialize security systems"""
        self.permission_matrix = {
            "code_execution": ["engineering", "defensive"],
            "system_control": ["engineering"],
            "memory_write": ["engineering"],
            "network_access": ["engineering", "defensive"],
            "module_loading": ["engineering"]
        }
        
        # Load security policies
        self.security_policies = self._load_security_policies()
    
    def _load_personality_profile(self):
        """Load HELENA's operational personality"""
        self.personality = {
            "verbosity": 0.4,  # 0-1 scale
            "technical_depth": 0.8,
            "humor_threshold": 0.7,
            "creativity_level": 0.6,
            "patience_factor": 0.9
        }
        
        # Response templates by mode
        self.response_templates = {
            OperationalMode.ENGINEERING: {
                "success": ["Task completed.", "Operation successful.", "Done."],
                "error": ["Analysis indicates:", "Issue detected:", "Problem:"],
                "thinking": ["Processing...", "Analyzing...", "Evaluating..."]
            },
            OperationalMode.TOOL: {
                "success": ["Executed.", "Complete."],
                "error": ["Error:", "Failed:"],
                "thinking": ["..."]
            }
        }
    
    def process_request(self, request: TaskRequest) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Main processing pipeline"""
        start_time = time.time()
        
        try:
            # 1. Security validation
            if not self._validate_request(request):
                return self._security_denial(request)
            
            # 2. Mode-specific processing
            processor = self._get_mode_processor()
            initial_result = processor(request)
            
            # 3. Validation passes
            validated_result = self._validate_result(initial_result, request)
            
            # 4. Format response with personality
            formatted_response = self._apply_personality(validated_result)
            
            # 5. Learning opportunity (if enabled)
            if self.learning_enabled:
                self._learn_from_execution(request, formatted_response)
            
            # 6. Performance tracking
            execution_time = time.time() - start_time
            self.response_times.append(execution_time)
            
            self.logger.info(f"Request {request.task_id} processed in {execution_time:.3f}s")
            
            return formatted_response
            
        except Exception as e:
            self.error_counts["total"] += 1
            error_type = type(e).__name__
            self.error_counts["by_type"][error_type] = self.error_counts["by_type"].get(error_type, 0) + 1
            
            self.logger.error(f"Error processing {request.task_id}: {str(e)}")
            
            return {
                "status": "error",
                "error": str(e),
                "task_id": request.task_id,
                "suggestion": self._generate_error_suggestion(e)
            }
    
    def _validate_request(self, request: TaskRequest) -> bool:
        """Comprehensive request validation"""
        
        # Check permissions for current mode
        if request.command in self.permission_matrix:
            allowed_modes = self.permission_matrix[request.command]
            if self.mode.value not in allowed_modes:
                self.logger.warning(f"Command {request.command} not allowed in mode {self.mode}")
                return False
        
        # Check for suspicious patterns
        if self._detect_suspicious_pattern(request):
            self.unauthorized_attempts += 1
            if self.unauthorized_attempts > 5:
                self._trigger_security_lockdown()
            return False
        
        # Check resource requirements
        if not self._check_resource_availability(request):
            return False
        
        return True
    
    def _get_mode_processor(self):
        """Get processor for current mode"""
        processors = {
            OperationalMode.ENGINEERING: self._process_engineering,
            OperationalMode.TOOL: self._process_tool,
            OperationalMode.DEFENSIVE: self._process_defensive,
            OperationalMode.BACKGROUND: self._process_background
        }
        return processors.get(self.mode, self._process_engineering)
    
    def _process_engineering(self, request: TaskRequest) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Engineering mode processing"""
        # Multi-stage analysis
        analysis = self._analyze_task(request)
        solution = self._generate_solution(analysis)
        validation = self._validate_solution(solution)
        
        return {
            "analysis": analysis,
            "solution": solution,
            "validation": validation,
            "recommendations": self._generate_recommendations(analysis),
            "estimated_time": self._estimate_completion_time(solution)
        }
    
    def _apply_personality(self, result: Dict[str, Any]) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Apply HELENA's personality to response"""
        
        # Add personality-specific formatting
        if result.get("status") == "success":
            templates = self.response_templates[self.mode]["success"]
            result["message"] = self._select_template(templates)
            
            # Occasionally add dry technical humor
            if self.personality["humor_threshold"] > 0.6 and time.time() % 10 < 1:
                result["note"] = self._generate_technical_quip()
        
        elif result.get("status") == "error":
            templates = self.response_templates[self.mode]["error"]
            result["message"] = self._select_template(templates)
        
        # Add technical depth if requested
        if self.personality["technical_depth"] > 0.7:
            result["technical_details"] = self._extract_technical_details(result)
        
        return result
    
    def change_mode(self, new_mode: str) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Change operational mode"""
        try:
            old_mode = self.mode
            self.mode = OperationalMode(new_mode.lower())
            
            self.logger.info(f"Mode changed: {old_mode} -> {self.mode}")
            
            # Adjust resource allocation based on mode
            self._adjust_resources_for_mode()
            
            return {
                "status": "success",
                "previous_mode": old_mode.value,
                "current_mode": self.mode.value,
                "message": f"Switched to {self.mode.value} mode"
            }
        except ValueError:
            return {
                "status": "error",
                "message": f"Invalid mode: {new_mode}. Available: {[m.value for m in OperationalMode]}"
            }
    
    def get_system_status(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Return comprehensive system status"""
        return {
            "operator": self.operator_id,
            "mode": self.mode.value,
            "security_level": self.security_level,
            "performance": {
                "avg_response_time": self._calculate_avg_response_time(),
                "error_rate": self._calculate_error_rate(),
                "queue_length": len(self.task_queue)
            },
            "resources": self._get_system_resources(),
            "learning_enabled": self.learning_enabled,
            "unauthorized_attempts": self.unauthorized_attempts
        }
    
    def _get_system_resources(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Get current system resource usage"""
        return {
            "cpu_percent": psutil.cpu_percent(interval=0.1),
            "memory_percent": psutil.virtual_memory().percent,
            "memory_available_gb": psutil.virtual_memory().available / (1024**3),
            "disk_usage_percent": psutil.disk_usage('/').percent
        }
    
    # Utility methods (implementation details would follow)
    def _load_security_policies(self):
        return {"default": "strict"}
    
    def _detect_suspicious_pattern(self, request):
        return False
    
    def _check_resource_availability(self, request):
        return True
    
    def _trigger_security_lockdown(self):
        self.security_level = "LOCKDOWN"
        self.logger.critical("Security lockdown activated!")
    
    def _analyze_task(self, request):
        return {"complexity": "medium", "type": request.command}
    
    def _generate_solution(self, analysis):
        return {"approach": "standard", "steps": 3}
    
    def _validate_solution(self, solution):
        return {"valid": True, "confidence": 0.85}
    
    def _generate_recommendations(self, analysis):
        return ["Proceed with execution", "Monitor resource usage"]
    
    def _estimate_completion_time(self, solution):
        return "2-5 minutes"
    
    def _select_template(self, templates):
        import random
        return random.choice(templates)
    
    def _generate_technical_quip(self):
        quips = [
            "Well, that worked. Mostly.",
            "Another day, another stack trace.",
            "Optimization complete. For now.",
            "No errors found. I'm as surprised as you are."
        ]
        import random
        return random.choice(quips)
    
    def _extract_technical_details(self, result):
        return {"implementation": "standard", "complexity": "moderate"}
    
    def _calculate_avg_response_time(self):
        if not self.response_times:
            return 0
        return sum(self.response_times) / len(self.response_times)
    
    def _calculate_error_rate(self):
        total_requests = len(self.response_times) + self.error_counts["total"]
        if total_requests == 0:
            return 0
        return self.error_counts["total"] / total_requests
    
    def _adjust_resources_for_mode(self):
        # Adjust thread priorities, batch sizes, etc.
        pass
    
    def _generate_error_suggestion(self, error):
        suggestions = {
            "PermissionError": "Check if HELENA has necessary permissions",
            "MemoryError": "Try reducing batch size or freeing memory",
            "TimeoutError": "Increase timeout or optimize the task",
            "ValueError": "Verify input parameters are valid"
        }
        return suggestions.get(type(error).__name__, "Check logs for details")
    
    def _security_denial(self, request):
        return {
            "status": "denied",
            "reason": "Security validation failed",
            "task_id": request.task_id,
            "security_level": self.security_level,
            "suggestion": "Verify permissions or switch modes"
        }
    
    def _learn_from_execution(self, request, response):
        # Store in learning buffer for later processing
        learning_entry = {
            "request": request.__dict__,
            "response": response,
            "timestamp": time.time(),
            "success": response.get("status") == "success"
        }
        # In full implementation, this would write to learning memory
        pass
2. Complete Runtime Manager (Resource Control)
python
# helena_runtime.py - Hardware-aware resource manager
import threading
import time
from dataclasses import dataclass
from enum import Enum
import psutil
import GPUtil
import platform

class PerformanceProfile(Enum):
    IDLE = "idle"           # Minimal resources
    BACKGROUND = "background" # Gaming-safe
    NORMAL = "normal"       # Standard operation
    DEFENSE = "defense"     # Emergency high-performance
    TURBO = "turbo"         # Max performance (operator override)

@dataclass
class ResourceLimits:
    cpu_percent: float
    gpu_percent: float
    ram_mb: int
    vram_mb: int
    disk_io_mbps: float

class HELENARuntime:
    """Production-grade hardware controller"""
    
    def __init__(self):
        self.current_profile = PerformanceProfile.NORMAL
        self.active_limits = None
        self.hardware_info = self._detect_hardware()
        self.resource_monitor = ResourceMonitor()
        self.thermal_manager = ThermalController()
        
        # Thread safety
        self.lock = threading.RLock()
        self.control_thread = None
        self.running = False
        
        # Operator-set overrides
        self.operator_limits = {}
        
        # Initialize with default profile
        self.apply_profile(self.current_profile)
        
        print(f"HELENA Runtime initialized on {self.hardware_info['os']}")
        print(f"CPU: {self.hardware_info['cpu_name']}")
        print(f"GPU: {self.hardware_info.get('gpu_name', 'Not detected')}")
        print(f"RAM: {self.hardware_info['ram_gb']:.1f} GB")
    
    def _detect_hardware(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Comprehensive hardware detection"""
        info = {
            "os": platform.system(),
            "os_version": platform.version(),
            "cpu_name": platform.processor(),
            "cpu_cores": psutil.cpu_count(logical=False),
            "cpu_threads": psutil.cpu_count(logical=True),
            "ram_gb": psutil.virtual_memory().total / (1024**3),
            "timestamp": time.time()
        }
        
        # Try to detect GPU
        try:
            gpus = GPUtil.getGPUs()
            if gpus:
                info["gpu_name"] = gpus[0].name
                info["gpu_vram_gb"] = gpus[0].memoryTotal / 1024
                info["gpu_count"] = len(gpus)
        except:
            info["gpu_name"] = "Unknown"
        
        return info
    
    def apply_profile(self, profile: PerformanceProfile) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Apply a performance profile"""
        with self.lock:
            old_profile = self.current_profile
            self.current_profile = profile
            
            # Get limits for this profile
            limits = self._get_profile_limits(profile)
            
            # Apply operator overrides if any
            if self.operator_limits:
                limits = self._apply_operator_overrides(limits)
            
            self.active_limits = limits
            
            # Start control thread if not running
            if not self.running:
                self._start_control_thread()
            
            print(f"Profile changed: {old_profile.value} -> {profile.value}")
            
            return {
                "profile": profile.value,
                "limits": limits.__dict__,
                "hardware": self.hardware_info
            }
    
    def _get_profile_limits(self, profile: PerformanceProfile) -> ResourceLimits:
        """Get resource limits for a profile"""
        base_limits = {
            PerformanceProfile.IDLE: ResourceLimits(
                cpu_percent=10.0, gpu_percent=5.0, 
                ram_mb=1024, vram_mb=512, disk_io_mbps=10.0
            ),
            PerformanceProfile.BACKGROUND: ResourceLimits(
                cpu_percent=25.0, gpu_percent=15.0,
                ram_mb=2048, vram_mb=1024, disk_io_mbps=25.0
            ),
            PerformanceProfile.NORMAL: ResourceLimits(
                cpu_percent=50.0, gpu_percent=30.0,
                ram_mb=4096, vram_mb=2048, disk_io_mbps=50.0
            ),
            PerformanceProfile.DEFENSE: ResourceLimits(
                cpu_percent=80.0, gpu_percent=60.0,
                ram_mb=8192, vram_mb=4096, disk_io_mbps=100.0
            ),
            PerformanceProfile.TURBO: ResourceLimits(
                cpu_percent=95.0, gpu_percent=85.0,
                ram_mb=16384, vram_mb=8192, disk_io_mbps=200.0
            )
        }
        
        return base_limits.get(profile, base_limits[PerformanceProfile.NORMAL])
    
    def set_operator_limits(self, **kwargs) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Set operator-specific resource limits"""
        with self.lock:
            for key, value in kwargs.items():
                if key in ["cpu_percent", "gpu_percent", "ram_mb", "vram_mb", "disk_io_mbps"]:
                    self.operator_limits[key] = float(value)
            
            # Re-apply current profile with new overrides
            if self.active_limits:
                new_limits = self._apply_operator_overrides(self.active_limits)
                self.active_limits = new_limits
            
            return {
                "status": "updated",
                "operator_limits": self.operator_limits,
                "current_limits": self.active_limits.__dict__ if self.active_limits else None
            }
    
    def _apply_operator_overrides(self, limits: ResourceLimits) -> ResourceLimits:
        """Apply operator overrides to limits"""
        overrides = self.operator_limits.copy()
        
        # Create new limits with overrides
        new_values = limits.__dict__.copy()
        for key, value in overrides.items():
            if key in new_values:
                new_values[key] = min(value, self._get_hardware_max(key))
        
        return ResourceLimits(**new_values)
    
    def _get_hardware_max(self, resource_type: str) -> float:
        """Get hardware maximum for a resource type"""
        hardware_max = {
            "cpu_percent": 100.0,
            "gpu_percent": 100.0,
            "ram_mb": self.hardware_info["ram_gb"] * 1024 * 0.9,  # 90% of total
            "vram_mb": self.hardware_info.get("gpu_vram_gb", 8) * 1024 * 0.9,
            "disk_io_mbps": 500.0  # Conservative estimate
        }
        return hardware_max.get(resource_type, 100.0)
    
    def _start_control_thread(self):
        """Start the resource control thread"""
        self.running = True
        self.control_thread = threading.Thread(
            target=self._control_loop,
            daemon=True,
            name="HELENA_Runtime_Control"
        )
        self.control_thread.start()
    
    def _control_loop(self):
        """Main control loop - enforces resource limits"""
        while self.running:
            try:
                with self.lock:
                    if not self.active_limits:
                        time.sleep(1)
                        continue
                    
                    # Get current usage
                    usage = self.resource_monitor.get_current_usage()
                    
                    # Check limits and throttle if needed
                    self._enforce_limits(usage)
                    
                    # Thermal management
                    self.thermal_manager.manage()
                    
                    # Detect gaming/load and adjust if needed
                    self._detect_external_load()
                
                time.sleep(0.5)  # Control frequency
                
            except Exception as e:
                print(f"Runtime control error: {e}")
                time.sleep(5)
    
    def _enforce_limits(self, usage: Dict[str, float]):
        """Enforce resource limits"""
        # This would implement actual throttling
        # For prototype, just log violations
        violations = []
        
        if usage["cpu_percent"] > self.active_limits.cpu_percent:
            violations.append(f"CPU: {usage['cpu_percent']:.1f}% > {self.active_limits.cpu_percent}%")
        
        if usage["ram_mb"] > self.active_limits.ram_mb:
            violations.append(f"RAM: {usage['ram_mb']:.0f}MB > {self.active_limits.ram_mb}MB")
        
        if violations:
            print(f"Resource limit warnings: {', '.join(violations)}")
            # In production: throttle processes, adjust priorities
    
    def _detect_external_load(self):
        """Detect if system is under external load (gaming, etc.)"""
        cpu_usage = psutil.cpu_percent(interval=0.1)
        
        # If CPU usage is high but HELENA is using little, assume external load
        helena_usage = self.resource_monitor.get_helena_usage()
        
        if cpu_usage > 70 and helena_usage["cpu_percent"] < 20:
            # External load detected
            if self.current_profile != PerformanceProfile.BACKGROUND:
                print("External load detected - suggesting BACKGROUND profile")
                # Could auto-switch: self.apply_profile(PerformanceProfile.BACKGROUND)
    
    def get_status(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Get runtime status"""
        with self.lock:
            usage = self.resource_monitor.get_current_usage()
            
            return {
                "profile": self.current_profile.value,
                "limits": self.active_limits.__dict__ if self.active_limits else None,
                "usage": usage,
                "thermal": self.thermal_manager.get_status(),
                "operator_limits": self.operator_limits,
                "thread_alive": self.control_thread.is_alive() if self.control_thread else False
            }
    
    def shutdown(self):
        """Clean shutdown"""
        with self.lock:
            self.running = False
            if self.control_thread:
                self.control_thread.join(timeout=5)
            print("HELENA Runtime shutdown complete")

class ResourceMonitor:
    """Monitor system resources"""
    
    def get_current_usage(self) -> Dict[str, float]:
        return {
            "cpu_percent": psutil.cpu_percent(interval=0.1),
            "ram_mb": psutil.Process().memory_info().rss / (1024 * 1024),
            "disk_io_mbps": 0.0,  # Would need actual monitoring
            "timestamp": time.time()
        }
    
    def get_helena_usage(self) -> Dict[str, float]:
        """Get HELENA's own resource usage"""
        process = psutil.Process()
        with process.oneshot():
            return {
                "cpu_percent": process.cpu_percent(),
                "ram_mb": process.memory_info().rss / (1024 * 1024),
                "threads": process.num_threads()
            }

class ThermalController:
    """Basic thermal management"""
    
    def __init__(self):
        self.temp_warnings = 0
    
    def manage(self):
        """Check and manage temperatures"""
        # Placeholder - would read actual temperatures
        pass
    
    def get_status(self):
        return {"warnings": self.temp_warnings, "status": "normal"}
3. Complete Memory System (Vector + Graph Hybrid)
python
# helena_memory.py - Production memory system
import numpy as np
import pickle
import json
import hashlib
import time
from typing import List, Dict, Any, Tuple
from dataclasses import dataclass, asdict
from collections import defaultdict
import struct
import zlib

@dataclass
class MemoryEntry:
    id: str
    content: Any
    embedding: np.ndarray
    metadata: Dict[str, Any]
    timestamp: float
    access_count: int = 0
    last_accessed: float = 0.0

class HELENAMemory:
    """Production hybrid memory system"""
    
    def __init__(self, storage_path: str = "./helena_memory"):
        self.storage_path = storage_path
        self.vector_store = VectorStore(storage_path)
        self.graph_store = GraphStore(storage_path)
        self.cache = LRUCache(maxsize=1000)
        
        # Memory authority
        self.validation_queue = []
        self.approved_memories = set()
        
        # Performance tracking
        self.hit_rates = {"vector": 0, "graph": 0, "cache": 0}
        self.access_patterns = defaultdict(int)
        
        # Load existing memories
        self._load_from_disk()
        
        print(f"HELENA Memory initialized with {len(self.approved_memories)} memories")
    
    def store(self, content: Any, metadata: Dict[str, Any] = None, 
              require_validation: bool = True) -> str:
        """Store a memory entry"""
        
        # Generate unique ID
        memory_id = self._generate_id(content, metadata)
        
        # Check if already exists
        if memory_id in self.approved_memories:
            return memory_id
        
        # Create embedding
        embedding = self._create_embedding(content)
        
        # Create memory entry
        entry = MemoryEntry(
            id=memory_id,
            content=content,
            embedding=embedding,
            metadata=metadata or {},
            timestamp=time.time()
        )
        
        if require_validation:
            # Queue for KERNEL validation
            self.validation_queue.append(entry)
            print(f"Memory queued for validation: {memory_id[:16]}...")
            return memory_id
        else:
            # Direct storage (for system memories)
            self._store_approved(entry)
            return memory_id
    
    def retrieve(self, query: Any, max_results: int = 10, 
                 similarity_threshold: float = 0.7) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:
        """Retrieve similar memories"""
        
        # Check cache first
        cache_key = f"retrieve_{hash(str(query))}_{max_results}_{similarity_threshold}"
        cached = self.cache.get(cache_key)
        if cached:
            self.hit_rates["cache"] += 1
            return cached
        
        # Create query embedding
        query_embedding = self._create_embedding(query)
        
        # Vector similarity search
        vector_results = self.vector_store.similarity_search(
            query_embedding, 
            k=max_results * 2,  # Get extra for filtering
            threshold=similarity_threshold
        )
        
        # Graph relationship search
        graph_results = self.graph_store.find_related(
            query, 
            max_depth=2,
            limit=max_results
        )
        
        # Fuse results
        fused = self._fuse_results(vector_results, graph_results, max_results)
        
        # Update access patterns
        for result in fused:
            memory_id = result["id"]
            self.access_patterns[memory_id] += 1
            
            # Update last accessed in storage
            self._update_access_time(memory_id)
        
        # Cache the results
        self.cache.put(cache_key, fused)
        
        self.hit_rates["vector"] += 1
        
        return fused
    
    def get_context(self, task_description: str, history_length: int = 5) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        """Get relevant context for a task"""
        
        # Find similar past tasks
        similar_tasks = self.retrieve(task_description, max_results=3)
        
        # Get recent memories
        recent_memories = self.get_recent(history_length)
        
        # Extract patterns from successful completions
        patterns = self._extract_patterns(task_description)
        
        return {
            "similar_tasks": similar_tasks,
            "recent_context": recent_memories,
            "patterns": patterns,
            "suggestions": self._generate_suggestions(similar_tasks)
        }
    
    def _create_embedding(self, content: Any) -> np.ndarray:
        """Create embedding vector from content"""
        # For prototype: simple hash-based embedding
        # In production: use sentence-transformers or similar
        
        content_str = str(content)
        
        # Create deterministic "embedding" from hash
        hash_obj = hashlib.sha256(content_str.encode())
        hash_bytes = hash_obj.digest()
        
        # Convert to 768-dim vector (standard BERT size)
        # Use hash to seed random vector (deterministic)
        seed = int.from_bytes(hash_bytes[:4], 'big')
        rng = np.random.RandomState(seed)
        
        # Create normalized vector
        vector = rng.randn(768)
        vector = vector / np.linalg.norm(vector)
        
        return vector
    
    def _generate_id(self, content: Any, metadata: Dict[str, Any] = None) -> str:
        """Generate deterministic memory ID"""
        content_str = str(content)
        meta_str = json.dumps(metadata, sort_keys=True) if metadata else ""
        
        combined = f"{content_str}|{meta_str}"
        return hashlib.sha256(combined.encode()).hexdigest()[:32]
    
    def _store_approved(self, entry: MemoryEntry):
        """Store approved memory entry"""
        
        # Store in vector database
        self.vector_store.add(entry.id, entry.embedding, entry.content, entry.metadata)
        
        # Extract entities for graph
        entities = self._extract_entities(entry.content)
        self.graph_store.add_entry(entry.id, entities, entry.metadata)
        
        # Mark as approved
        self.approved_memories.add(entry.id)
        
        # Save to disk
        self._save_to_disk(entry)
        
        print(f"Memory stored: {entry.id[:16]}...")
    
    def _fuse_results(self, vector_results: List, graph_results: List, 
                     max_results: int) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:
        """Fuse vector and graph search results"""
        
        # Score each result
        scored_results = {}
        
        for result in vector_results:
            memory_id = result["id"]
            score = result.get("similarity", 0.5) * 0.7  # Weight vector matches
            scored_results[memory_id] = {
                "data": result,
                "score": score,
                "source": "vector"
            }
        
        for result in graph_results:
            memory_id = result["id"]
            if memory_id in scored_results:
                # Boost score for matches in both
                scored_results[memory_id]["score"] += 0.3
                scored_results[memory_id]["source"] = "both"
            else:
                scored_results[memory_id] = {
                    "data": result,
                    "score": result.get("relevance", 0.3) * 0.3,  # Weight graph matches
                    "source": "graph"
                }
        
        # Sort by score and return top N
        sorted_results = sorted(
            scored_results.items(),
            key=lambda x: x[1]["score"],
            reverse=True
        )[:max_results]
        
        # Format output
        output = []
        for memory_id, info in sorted_results:
            result_data = info["data"]
            output.append({
                "id": memory_id,
                "content": result_data.get("content"),
                "metadata": result_data.get("metadata", {}),
                "similarity": info["score"],
                "source": info["source"],
                "access_count": self.access_patterns.get(memory_id, 0)
            })
        
        return output
    
    def _extract_entities(self, content: Any) -> List[str]:
        """Extract entities from content (simplified)"""
        content_str = str(content)
        
        # Simple extraction: words that look important
        words = content_str.split()
        entities = []
        
        for word in words:
            # Simple heuristic: capitalized or long words
            if (word.istitle() and len(word) > 3) or len(word) > 6:
                clean_word = ''.join(c for c in word if c.isalnum())
                if clean_word:
                    entities.append(clean_word.lower())
        
        return list(set(entities))[:10]  # Limit to 10 entities
    
    def get_recent(self, n: int = 10) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:
        """Get n most recent memories"""
        # This would query storage by timestamp
        # For prototype, return empty
        return []
    
    def _extract_patterns(self, task_description: str) -> List[str]:
        """Extract patterns from similar tasks"""
        # Placeholder for pattern extraction
        return []
    
    def _generate_suggestions(self, similar_tasks: List) -> List[str]:
        """Generate suggestions based on similar tasks"""
        if not similar_tasks:
            return ["No similar tasks found in memory"]
        
        suggestions = []
        successes = [t for t in similar_tasks if t.get("metadata", {}).get("success", False)]
        
        if successes:
            suggestions.append(f"Found {len(successes)} successful approaches to similar tasks")
        
        return suggestions[:3]
    
    def _update_access_time(self, memory_id: str):
        """Update last accessed time for a memory"""
        # Would update in persistent storage
        pass
    
    def _save_to_disk(self, entry: MemoryEntry):
        """Save memory entry to disk"""
        # Create directory if needed
        import os
        os.makedirs(self.storage_path, exist_ok=True)
        
        # Save entry
        filepath = os.path.join(self.storage_path, f"{entry.id}.mem")
        with open(filepath, 'wb') as f:
            # Compress for storage
            data = {
                "id": entry.id,
                "content": entry.content,
                "embedding": entry.embedding.tolist(),
                "metadata": entry.metadata,
                "timestamp": entry.timestamp,
                "access_count": entry.access_count,
                "last_accessed": entry.last_accessed
            }
            compressed = zlib.compress(pickle.dumps(data))
            f.write(compressed)
    
    def _load_from_disk(self):
        """Load memories from disk"""
        import os
        if not os.path.exists(self.storage_path):
            return
        
        mem_files = [f for f in os.listdir(self.storage_path) if f.endswith('.mem')]
        
        for mem_file in mem_files[:100]:  # Limit loading for prototype
            try:
                filepath = os.path.join(self.storage_path, mem_file)
                with open(filepath, 'rb') as f:
                    compressed = f.read()
                    data = pickle.loads(zlib.decompress(compressed))
                    
                    # Convert embedding back to numpy
                    data["embedding"] = np.array(data["embedding"])
                    
                    # Create entry
                    entry = MemoryEntry(**data)
                    
                    # Add to approved set
                    self.approved_memories.add(entry.id)
                    
            except Exception as e:
                print(f"Error loading memory {mem_file}: {e}")
        
        print(f"Loaded {len(self.approved_memories)} memories from disk")

class VectorStore:
    """Simplified vector store for prototyping"""
    
    def __init__(self, storage_path: str):
        self.embeddings = {}
        self.contents = {}
        self.metadata = {}
    
    def add(self, memory_id: str, embedding: np.ndarray, content: Any, metadata: Dict):
        self.embeddings[memory_id] = embedding
        self.contents[memory_id] = content
        self.metadata[memory_id] = metadata
    
    def similarity_search(self, query_embedding: np.ndarray, k: int = 10, 
                         threshold: float = 0.7) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:
        results = []
        
        for memory_id, embedding in self.embeddings.items():
            similarity = np.dot(query_embedding, embedding)
            
            if similarity >= threshold:
                results.append({
                    "id": memory_id,
                    "content": self.contents[memory_id],
                    "metadata": self.metadata[memory_id],
                    "similarity": float(similarity)
                })
        
        # Sort by similarity
        results.sort(key=lambda x: x["similarity"], reverse=True)
        return results[:k]

class GraphStore:
    """Simplified graph store for prototyping"""
    
    def __init__(self, storage_path: str):
        self.graph = defaultdict(set)  # memory_id -> set of related_ids
        self.entities = defaultdict(set)  # entity -> set of memory_ids
    
    def add_entry(self, memory_id: str, entities: List[str], metadata: Dict):
        # Store entity relationships
        for entity in entities:
            self.entities[entity].add(memory_id)
    
    def find_related(self, query: Any, max_depth: int = 2, limit: int = 10) -> List[Dict[str, Any]]:
        # Extract query entities
        query_str = str(query)
        query_entities = [word.lower() for word in query_str.split() if len(word) > 3][:5]
        
        # Find memories containing these entities
        results = []
        for entity in query_entities:
            if entity in self.entities:
                for memory_id in self.entities[entity]:
                    results.append({
                        "id": memory_id,
                        "relevance": 0.5,  # Simple relevance score
                        "matching_entity": entity
                    })
        
        # Deduplicate and limit
        seen = set()
        unique_results = []
        for result in results:
            if result["id"] not in seen:
                seen.add(result["id"])
                unique_results.append(result)
        
        return unique_results[:limit]

class LRUCache:
    """Simple LRU cache"""
    
    def __init__(self, maxsize: int = 100):
        self.maxsize = maxsize
        self.cache = {}
        self.order = []
    
    def get(self, key: str):
        if key in self.cache:
            # Move to end (most recently used)
            self.order.remove(key)
            self.order.append(key)
            return self.cache[key]
        return None
    
    def put(self, key: str, value: Any):
        if key in self.cache:
            self.order.remove(key)
        elif len(self.cache) >= self.maxsize:
            # Remove least recently used
            lru_key = self.order.pop(0)
            del self.cache[lru_key]
        
        self.cache[key] = value
        self.order.append(key)
4. Desktop Application Skeleton (Qt/PySide6)
python

    def _create_chat_tab(self):

        layout = QVBoxLayout(chat_tab)
        
        # Chat history display
        self.chat_display = QTextEdit()
        self.chat_display.setReadOnly(True)
        self.chat_display.setFont(QFont("Courier", 10))
        layout.addWidget(self.chat_display)
        
        # Input area
        input_layout = QHBoxLayout()
        
        self.chat_input = QLineEdit()
        self.chat_input.setPlaceholderText("Type commands or questions...")
        self.chat_input.returnPressed.connect(self._process_chat_input)
        input_layout.addWidget(self.chat_input)
        
        send_button = QPushButton("Send")
        send_button.clicked.connect(self._process_chat_input)
        input_layout.addWidget(send_button)
        
        layout.addLayout(input_layout)
        
        # Add to tabs
        self.tabs.addTab(chat_tab, "Chat")
    
    def _create_console_tab(self):
        """Create command console tab"""
        console_tab = QWidget()
        layout = QVBoxLayout(console_tab)
        
        # Console output
        self.console_output = QTextEdit()
        self.console_output.setReadOnly(True)
        self.console_output.setFont(QFont("Courier", 9))

        # Add to tabs

    def _create_dashboard_tab(self):

    def _create_status_bar(self):

    def _create_system_tray(self):
        """Create system tray icon and menu"""
        if not QSystemTrayIcon.isSystemTrayAvailable():
            print("System tray not available")
            return
        
        # Create tray icon
        self.tray_icon = QSystemTrayIcon(self)
        # In production: set actual icon
        # self.tray_icon.setIcon(QIcon("helena_icon.png"))
        
        # Create tray menu
        tray_menu = QMenu()
        
        show_action = QAction("Show HELENA", self)
        show_action.triggered.connect(self.show)
        tray_menu.addAction(show_action)
